The authorities of the French Concession

Explanation for the Arrest of Koreans 176

Regarding the arrest of Koreans in the French Concession, various opinions have appeared in the newspapers. The French authorities have provided an explanation: On the day of the incident in Hongkou Park, the French police were informed by the Japanese police that (1) the perpetrator arrested on the spot at the time of the incident was Yin Bong-gil, a Korean living in the French Concession; (2) this person confessed that the criminal intent and preparation were all in the French Concession. On the same day, the Japanese consul personally confirmed this statement to the French consul and requested the French police to assist in detaining 26 Koreans living in the French Concession. These Koreans were wanted by the Japanese judicial authorities with arrest warrants for conspiracy. It should be noted that under these circumstances, there is no extradition issue. In fact, according to existing treaties, any country that has jurisdiction over its own nationals residing in China can naturally execute arrest warrants issued by its judicial authorities within the borders of various concessions. This is due to complete rights. The judicial authorities only have the obligation to request assistance from the concession police. On April 29th and 30th, 11 Koreans were detained in the French Concession, all with formal arrest warrants issued by the Japanese judicial authorities. No one gave up their Korean nationality, did not recognize the jurisdiction of the Japanese court over themselves, and no one claimed to be a Chinese national. During the search on April 30th, Xu Xianda, a Chinese who was in a Korean's home, was taken to the police station for investigation by French police officers. As no evidence of a crime was found, he was released. All statements contrary to the above announcement are unfounded.

Literary Inquisition in the French Concession 177

▲ Wei Yan Daily Accusation Case ▲ Sentencing scheduled for the 14th Fan Shuheng, a Hubei native, founded the Wei Yan Daily in the French Concession. Because he had not registered with the authorities in advance, and the published articles contained many attacks, and the newspaper did not specify the place of publication, the political department of the French police found out the location of the printing house and the editorial department, sent detectives to 61 Xiafei Fang and 573 Avenue Edward VII, and arrested Fan Zhiping and Chen Linyi, the owner of the printing house, seized newspapers and two plates of lead type, took them to the police station, and transferred them to the Second Special Court. The police filed a lawsuit according to the Publishing Law and the French Consul's Order No. 187. After the interrogation, Chen was ordered to pay a bail of 500 yuan, and Fan was remanded in custody pending verification. The details have been recorded in the newspapers. At 3:00 p.m. yesterday, Judge Zhang Chaozuo visited the Second Criminal Court for further interrogation. According to Fan Zhiping, he worked as a proofreader in the newspaper for three weeks, and there were three people in the editorial department. He did not know who was in charge. Chen confessed that Fan Shuheng came to negotiate for printing, which had been printed for three months. A contract was signed with no time limit, and the printing fee was 10 yuan per day. He did not know anything else. The court ordered the debate to begin. After the police lawyer Gu Shouxi debated with the lawyer hired by the defendant, the court declared the debate over and scheduled the sentencing for the afternoon of the 14th. Fan Zhiping was ordered to pay a bail of 200 yuan, and Chen was released on the original bail pending instructions.

Labor-Management Disputes at Commercial Press Reach Extremes 178

▲ Employees Refused to Collect Wages Yesterday ▲ Opposing Layoffs and Hoping for Resumption of Work Since the Commercial Press's Zhabei General Factory was destroyed by Japanese bombing, the company, due to huge losses, could not maintain operations and stopped the business of the Qipanjie Distribution Office as well. A plan was formulated to lay off employees, and from 9:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 2:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. yesterday, severance pay was started to be issued to all employees of the General Affairs Department and the Distribution Office at 24 Ningbo Road to implement layoffs. However, the employees believed that the company's layoffs this time were illegal and immediately organized an Employee Hardship Relief Committee to discuss countermeasures and vowed to oppose it. Yesterday, when the company issued severance pay, an advisory group was organized to go to the payment place to advise the employees who went there to collect it. Therefore, although the company prepared a large sum of money yesterday, most people were unwilling to collect it. Labor and management seem to have reached extremes. The various situations are recorded separately below. ▲ Amount to Be Paid The company seems determined to lay off employees this time. The severance pay and compensation (i.e., retirement salary fund) to be paid to the employees and the withdrawal of the current and special savings have long been formulated and announced. The amounts to be paid are: (1) compensation fund (17.8% of the original amount of each retirement salary); (2) severance pay (regardless of the original salary, half a month's salary will be paid uniformly). If the income of the above two items is less than 50 yuan, it will be supplemented to 50 yuan. If the income of apprentices is less than 25 yuan, it will be supplemented to 25 yuan; (3) special savings (all refunded at once); (4) current savings (if the deposit is less than 200 yuan, it will be withdrawn at once; if it is more than 200 yuan, it will be allowed to be refunded in installments within four months). ▲ Results of Payment The Board of Directors of the Commercial Press decided to issue the various payments to the employees of the General Affairs Department, Printing Factory, Letterpress Department, Gluing Department, Parts Department, Gravure Department, Song Style Department, Tibetan Plate Department, Electroplating Steel Plate Department, and the first binding department, decoration department, cutting department, museum department, oil department, drawing department, full plate department, carpentry department, and the various departments of the Distribution Office from 9:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 2:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. yesterday at 24 Ningbo Road, including severance pay, retirement salary, and current and special savings. However, all the employees of the company did not go to collect it. One or two workers who went to collect the money were also politely persuaded back by the advisory group organized by the employees. ▲ News from the Company The Aftermath Office of the Commercial Press, under the order of the Board of Directors, began to issue the retirement salary fund, an additional half month's salary, and all special savings that the employees should receive yesterday. The payment place was located at the old site of the Shanghai Bank at 24 Ningbo Road. Because the Employee Committee posted a serious notice prohibiting people from going to collect the money, and people were blocking and intimidating along the way, although there were nearly a thousand employees staying in Shanghai, and the company was paying by department on a daily basis, no less than two hundred people had already collected the money yesterday. Those who were eager to collect the money and return home but were blocked went to the Aftermath Office of the company on Sichuan Road to complain, and some inquired about the situation by telephone and entrusted others to collect the money in writing. The company also issued the money accordingly. The company will still be issuing the money at the original location today and tomorrow. ▲ Employee Advisory Group Yesterday was the first day for the Commercial Press to issue employee severance pay and implement layoffs. The employee side was really afraid that there were one or two ignorant workers who did not understand the truth and went to collect the money, so they specially organized an advisory group and stationed them near the payment place of the company at 24 Ningbo Road. When encountering employees going to collect the money, they would come forward to explain the great righteousness and persuade them not to go to collect it, destroying the spirit of cooperation among the workers and harming themselves and others. It is estimated that from 9:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. yesterday, about ten people were politely persuaded back by the advisory group. ▲ Notice from the Relief Committee The company is starting illegal layoffs today and depriving us of most of the benefits we deserve. This committee vows not to recognize it. I hope that our colleagues and temporarily hired colleagues will not go to collect the money, so as not to harm themselves and others. This is hereby announced. The Employee Hardship Relief Committee of the Commercial Press. ▲ Four Workers Arrested Datong News Agency reported that the Commercial Press started issuing retirement salary payments at its office at 24 Ningbo Road yesterday. However, because the Employee Aftermath Committee had issued a notice opposing it, very few people went to collect the money. It was unexpected that at around 2:00 p.m., four workers from the printing factory, Hu Jialong, Zhu Guizhen, Wang A'jin (male), and Zhang Xiuling (female), went to the office to inquire about something, and a dispute immediately occurred, leading to their arrest by the post police and taken to the Sima Road Police Station. After interrogation, it was found that there was no other relationship, and they were released at 3:30 p.m. Fearing accidents, the company requested the Public Concession to send many Chinese and Western police officers to protect the office.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Sells Japanese Trademark Collection on Behalf of Others 187

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce has received letters from overseas Chinese chambers of commerce and anti-Japanese associations in various provinces, cities, and counties, stating that many cannot identify Japanese goods trademarks and requesting investigation. Therefore, the Commercial Monthly of the chamber has agreed with the Publishing Department of the Xinsheng News Agency at 280 Wangping Street to sell the Japanese Trademark Collection published by the agency on behalf of others. This book collects Japanese trademarks, totaling 65 categories, with 1,200 illustrations and 3,000 product names. All Japanese goods sold in China are fully recorded. It is inscribed by Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, and the preface is by Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, and Yan E'sheng, Secretary. It is printed on high-quality Lian Shi paper with a fine print in a thick volume of 400 pages. Each volume only recovers half of the cost, a practical foreign currency of 1 yuan and 5 jiao, and an additional 2 jiao for postage for outside areas. It is the only reliable publication for identifying Japanese goods.

Repercussions of the Eviction Notice for Xiyongren Lane 188

The houses in Xiyongren Lane, Julai Road, French Concession, are managed by Xinglong Company. There are more than thirty buildings in total, built no more than fifteen years ago. The houses are very sturdy. Since the tenants moved in, the rent has been increased over the years. Last spring, the rent was raised again. However, the landlord wanted to raise the rent again in August, which was rejected by the tenants. Unexpectedly, because the tenants refused to increase the rent, the landlord notified all tenants in May of this year to move out completely before mid-June in the lunar calendar, in order to start reconstruction, etc. Hearing this news, the tenants panicked and convened a meeting of all tenants in the lane at 3 pm yesterday to discuss countermeasures. More than thirty people attended, and Shen Liangcai was elected as chairman. The following resolutions were made: (1) Organize a tenants' association; (2) Publicly appoint Shen Liangcai, Xinjihao, Shengyuanhao, Huangjinj, and Minglishe as five representatives responsible for handling negotiations; (3) First, the association will send a letter to Xinglong Company denying the reconstruction notice; (4) Send a letter to the Shanghai Citizens' Rent Reduction Movement Committee, various rent reduction associations in the French Concession, and the Xiqu Business Federation, etc., stating the situation of the landlord's failure to increase rent and using demolition as a pretext, advocating fairness and seeking unanimous assistance; (5) Investigate the statement in the notice that the 工部局 (French Municipal Council) has sent a letter ordering the demolition of the houses. The association should send a letter to the French 工部局 to inquire whether this is the case. If it is true, the bureau should be requested to consider the post-war economic downturn and the fact that the houses are sturdy, and withdraw the order; (6) Hire Li Ming, a lawyer, as legal counsel; (7) All expenses will be borne by everyone. The meeting adjourned after the resolutions were made.

University Student Assaults His Parents 190

▲ Son Refutes His Father's Accusations as Untrue

Cheng Zhongjun, also known as Axing, the third son of Cheng Weizu, a Songjiang native who used to work as a secretary in the Ministry of Justice, residing at No. 2 Hongyi Lane, Maisaiertiluo Road, French Concession, is twenty-one years old this year. He used to study at St. John's University and is now studying at the Law School of Soochow University. He is naturally stubborn and violent and has treated his parents with indecent behavior. Recently, he has neglected his studies and often provokes trouble at home. At 2 am on the 6th of this month, he quarreled over a trivial matter and drove his mother and grandmother out of the house. Then, he smashed the bed and cooking utensils of his mother and cut the telephone line. The next day, Cheng returned home and scolded him, but Axing even attacked his father. He was stopped by his family. Later, Cheng reported to the Xiafei Road Police Station, which sent detective Tian Shiqing to arrest Axing and seize the destroyed evidence, and brought them to the police station. Yesterday, he was transferred to the Fourth Criminal Court of the Second Special Court, where Judge Wu Fanglian presided over the trial. First, the police lawyer Fei Xizhen explained the case, prosecuting him according to Articles 293, Section 2, and 332 of the Criminal Law. According to Cheng Weizu's accusation, his son Axing has recently neglected his studies and gets up at 3 or 4 pm every day. He often treats his mother violently at home. The night before, when he was not at home, Axing drove his mother and grandmother out and smashed objects. Now, his maternal uncle is persuading him. He requested a postponement until Axing repents, apologizes to his mother, and is released on bail to prevent indecent behavior in the future. Then, he can withdraw the charges. He hopes that his son will reform himself. Axing argued that the plaintiff's accusations were untrue. He had been accused of the same facts before, and the court dismissed the case. He is studying at the Law School and knows the dignity of the law. How dare he assault his parents? However, the relationship between his father and son is usually not good, while the relationship between mother and son has always been harmonious. There was no destruction of property. If the court wants him to post bail, he can ask Mr. Shi and Mr. Huang to provide bail. He asked the court to see the truth. After the court lectured the defendant, it ordered a postponement to the 18th for further hearing.

▲ Accusing a Newspaper Reporter of Being a Communist Bandit

After the interruption of traffic on the Jinpu (Nanjing-Pukou) and Huning (Shanghai-Nanjing) Railways, the number of passengers on inland steam launches traveling to various places along the Suzhou River suddenly increased. Conclusion of the Case of a Steam Launch Hitting and Sinking a Woman 192

▲ One Yuan for Coffin Cloth ▲ 100 Yuan for Compensation

Xu Linsheng, a ferryman for the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company, overloaded his ferry with female workers, exceeding the passenger limit and had insufficient lighting, which led to it being hit and sunk by the Jingguang steam launch, resulting in the drowning of 26 female workers. At that time, the Water Patrol Police Station detained Xu Linsheng and Wang A'mei, the owner of the Jingguang, and handed them over to the District Court. Prosecutor Yang Qi has already dismissed the charges against Wang A'mei and filed a public lawsuit against Xu Linsheng. The case was concluded yesterday. Xu Linsheng was sentenced to four months in prison and had to pay one yuan for each of the deceased female workers, totaling 26 yuan, for coffin cloth. In addition, the prosecutor ordered the Customs to pay 100 yuan for each body as compensation. However, the coffin and burial costs for the deceased were still less than half of the amount. Fortunately, the Nanyang Company donated more than 130 yuan per body to make up for the shortfall, showing compassion.

Meeting of the Board of Directors and Supervisors of the Second District Electrical and Plumbing Workers' Union 193

The newly elected board of directors and supervisors of the Second District Electrical and Plumbing Workers' Union have been recorded in this newspaper. The Chinese Taoist Association Opens a Free Clinic 194

The Hongdao Free School, run by the Chinese Taoist Association, has been registered by the Education Bureau and has achieved remarkable results. Even with the impact of the war, it continues unabated, so that children from poor families do not lose the opportunity to study. Its spirit of doing things is commendable. The board of directors of the association believes that the climate is changing from spring to summer, and epidemics are likely to occur. In order to prevent this, a free clinic has been set up in the association's hall on Qiaojiazhai Road, Dainanmen. Xie Qianggong and other directors have organized a trial operation and invited Confucian doctor Gu Linzhou to temporarily serve as assistant to the free clinic. The clinic will open on the 15th of this month, from 8 am to 12 pm every day. All poor and sick people who cannot afford medical treatment can go to register for consultation. If the clinic is busy in the future and funds are available, it will be expanded successively, more Chinese and Western doctors will be hired, and medicines will be purchased and distributed to achieve perfection. Because most of the area near the association is inhabited by hard-working poor people, the initiation of this free clinic is also good news for the charity world.

Central Bank Inspection Report 196

▲ 124th Central Bank Issuance Reserve

The 124th Inspection Report on the Central Bank's Issuance Reserve states that, in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this association is responsible for inspecting the reserve fund for the issuance of convertible notes of this bank. On May 10, 1932, Supervisor Wang Yihou conducted the 124th inspection at the Issuance Bureau of this bank. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: (A) Total amount of convertible notes issued: 27,460,012 silver dollars, including 24,766,302 silver dollar notes and 2,693,710 subsidiary notes. Total amount of convertible note reserve: 27,460,012 silver dollars, including 21,920,736 silver dollars in cash reserve, of which 18,886,123.45 silver dollars are stored in the issuance vault of this bank, 1,384,865 silver dollars are stored in branches in various ports, and 1,649,747.55 silver dollars are stored in other banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 5,539,276 silver dollars. (B) Total amount of Customs Gold convertible notes issued: 375,000 yuan. Total amount of Customs Gold convertible note reserve: 375,000 yuan, including US$150,000 stored in other banks in this port, converted to Customs Gold at the fixed price of 0.40. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Note Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash exceeds 60% and the guarantee is less than 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is hereby made. May 10, 1932, Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank.

Ren Lupi's Funeral Held Yesterday 200

Ren Lupi, the deceased district chief of the Sixth District Public Security Bureau, passed away at the age of only 41. He left behind an elderly father and two sons. He was hardworking and honest, and his family was poor. All circles mourned his death. Yesterday was the day of his funeral. The procession departed from his residence in Minhou Lane at 1:00 pm, passing through Jing'an Temple and Caojiadu, and was buried in the Yong'an Cemetery on Huobilan Road in West Shanghai. Many people from all walks of life held the ropes and sent him off. The Public Security Headquarters sent a military band and a small team of the police brigade. The third district branch of the Caojiadu Citizens' Federation, the Bao Wei Tuan, the Fire Brigade, and the Yong Yi Tang and other groups offered plaques and couplets in recognition of Ren's tireless efforts to protect the local area. In addition to sending off the military band, banquets were also set up at the Bao Wei Tuan and Fire Brigade gates for roadside sacrifices. Zhang Mingqin, the newly appointed district chief of the Sixth District, and all the patrol officers and chiefs of police also lined up to send him off, making it a grand occasion.

Letter 203

To the Editor:

According to Mr. Cheng Qin'guan, manager of the Dafaxiang Hardware Store, to whom our firm represents, on February 4 of this year, an article was published in the news section of your newspaper stating that unscrupulous merchants were providing food to the enemy and have now been investigated. The article stated that Cheng Qin'guan of Cheng Daxiang Rice Store at No. 50 Wuchang Road, at this time of the Sino-Japanese war, dared to be so unconscionable as to continuously provide rice to the Japanese army, and that an employee of the store, moved by patriotic indignation, went to report the crime, and someone was sent to investigate, etc. However, this is a fabricated fact, entirely the result of an employee named Chen colluding with Zhang to extort money and, failing to do so, falsely accusing him out of revenge. It is, in fact, a defamation of our client's reputation. Before the outbreak of the war, Shanghai merchants were legitimately engaged in various businesses. After the outbreak of the war, they should avoid dangerous areas. How dare the employee Chen, unable to defraud him, retaliate by making reckless statements in the name of the public? This concerns Mr. Cheng's reputation. Our client has always admired your newspaper's prestigious reputation, and although you record everything you hear, everything must be based on facts. If you investigate whether Cheng Daxiang Rice Store exists at that location, the truth will be revealed. Since it is a fabricated and retaliatory act, we request a correction to clarify the truth. Based on the facts provided by our client, our lawyer has prepared this letter requesting a correction. We respectfully request the attention of the editor of the Shenbao.

Lawyer Ge Zhaoji

Views on Tutelage and Constitutionalism (Continued) 205

Wang Zao Shi's third reason against ending tutelage is that past constitutionalism did not achieve good results, so constitutionalism should not be implemented now. But has constitutionalism ever truly been implemented in the past? Wang himself said that Yuan Shikai and the Northern Warlord bureaucratic politicians destroyed constitutionalism. Therefore, the poor results were the result of not implementing constitutionalism. If constitutionalism had been implemented, how could there have been Yuan Shikai's proclamation as emperor, the dissolution of the parliament, the infighting of the warlords, and Sun Yat-sen becoming an extraordinary president in Guangdong? These facts prove the necessity of constitutionalism and the sins of those who destroy and oppose constitutionalism. Wang and Yu scolded the bureaucratic politicians who destroyed constitutionalism earlier, so why did they become bureaucratic politicians who opposed the implementation of constitutionalism later?

The fourth reason against ending tutelage is that some people who advocate constitutionalism now are former bureaucratic politicians who are not worthy of talking about constitutionalism. Whether China should end tutelage and implement constitutionalism now is one matter; whether former bureaucratic politicians are worthy of talking about constitutionalism is another matter. If China should implement constitutionalism, then it should be implemented no matter who talks about it. One cannot reject the idea because of the person, nor can one abstain from eating for fear of choking. One should separate the matter from the person. Moreover, former bureaucratic politicians may not be worse than current bureaucratic politicians.

The above arguments against ending tutelage are the common opinions of Wang and Yu, but Wang's statements are more clear and organized. In addition, some of Wang and Yu's words need to be corrected separately.

For example, Wang Jingwei said: "...At that time, the Provisional Constitution and the Constitution were both created by Kuomintang party members to restrain Yuan Shikai and consolidate the foundation of the Republic of China. Therefore, to overthrow the Kuomintang, they had to destroy constitutionalism." From this, it seems that the Kuomintang and Wang himself originally advocated constitutionalism and believed that those who destroyed constitutionalism were wrong. So why does Wang now oppose constitutionalism and scold those who advocate constitutionalism? Is the level of the general public now inferior to that of the early Republic of China? Or is it because the Kuomintang did not have political power before, so they created the Provisional Constitution and the Constitution to restrain Yuan Shikai? Now that they have gained political power, they scold those who advocate constitutionalism to restrain one-party rule and consolidate the Republic of China?

For example, Wang said: "...China still does not have constitutionalism, but what is the reason for this? This is because since the Republic of China, constitutionalism has been destroyed by them once, twice, and three times." During the Beijing government era, the bureaucratic politicians of the past cannot but bear some responsibility for the failure to implement constitutionalism; but the biggest obstacle was still Yuan Shikai and his remaining Northern Warlords, which Wang must recognize. And since the Kuomintang came to power, who is to blame for completely abandoning constitutionalism and changing the Republic of China to a party-state? Former bureaucratic politicians, at best, only destroyed constitutionalism. The current bureaucratic officials fundamentally do not want constitutionalism. Why is Wang clear in blaming others but dim in blaming himself?

For example, Wang said: "Since the beginning of tutelage in the 17th or 18th year of the Republic of China, there have only been three years. If there were no internal disputes, it would certainly have been done better. But given the size of China, its vastness, and the complexity of the situation, no one can completely do well in China in one or two years." In fact, since the Kuomintang's dictatorship, there have been six years. Given the size of China, we certainly should not hope to do everything completely well. However, the Kuomintang, now claiming to be a revolutionary party and using tutelage as a pretext, should at least do better than the Beijing government era to be qualified to scold others and to be qualified for tutelage. But may I ask, in diplomacy and domestic affairs, where can it compare to the past? Only the degree of corruption, the speed of internal strife, and the means of betraying the country are worse than before. Before Wang came to power, he attacked the Nanjing government for not achieving results more fiercely than anyone else. Now that Wang is in power, he supports the Nanjing government more fiercely than anyone else. Why is there such inconsistency? In fact, the Kuomintang is doing badly, and there are facts to prove it. Wang himself certainly understands this. The so-called internal disputes are all caused by your Kuomintang civil and military comrades themselves, all caused by the enlightened and farsighted who claim to be under tutelage. Wang's own flip-flopping is especially responsible and has nothing to do with us common people. Wang has no remorse and does not admit that the Kuomintang and himself have the slightest fault, as if he still wants to put the blame on the heads of our general public. How can this be said?

As for Yu Youren's words, there are even more inexplicable things. Here are a few simple pointers to the biggest mistakes: (1) As Sun Zhesheng said, "Mr. Yu's biggest mistake is his inability to admit the past mistakes of our party (the Kuomintang), believing that our party is still a sound revolutionary party. Therefore, he believes that our party's ability to lead the Chinese national revolution is based on objective facts." In fact, the Kuomintang is now occupied by warlord bureaucratic politicians and cannot lead the revolution. In fact, it is increasingly becoming counter-revolutionary and is being revolutionised. (2) "The constitutionalism sought by our party is revolutionary constitutionalism, a revolutionary constitution; and only the revolutionary people can accept it and implement it." After reading all the political science books and checking all the dictionaries of various countries, I am afraid that I cannot find the term "revolutionary constitutionalism." Anyone with a little political common sense knows that "constitutionalism" and "revolution" are incompatible. Under constitutionalism, revolution is not allowed; under revolution, constitutionalism is not considered. As for the "revolutionary people," they do not need any constitution or constitutionalism. The reason why we advocate ending tutelage and implementing constitutionalism today is that the unrevolutionary people are demanding unrevolutionary constitutionalism. If we really start a revolution, how can we talk about constitutionalism? At that time, even if the Kuomintang hurriedly prepares for constitutionalism like the late Qing Dynasty, we will certainly ignore it as the late President did. As for "accepting it and implementing it," it is even more out of the question. (3) "During this national crisis, it is a matter of course to allow the people to supervise politics and guide them to participate in politics." If the people's participation in politics is a matter of course, then tutelage should be ended and democracy should be implemented. But Yu says that the people's participation in politics is a matter of course, while also saying that the Kuomintang's tutelage is a matter of course. Which one is a matter of course? Please tell me, Mr. Yu. In fact, with party rule, there is no democracy; with democratic politics, there is no one-party dictatorship. Both cannot be a matter of course at the same time. (4) "The party uses the form of democratic centralism to govern the party and politics, fearing that it will be too scattered, so why take the empty name of democratic politics and suffer the real disaster of disorganization?" From this point of view, Yu fundamentally does not believe in democratic politics, believing that democratic organization is scattered and harmful, and that the party uses it with fear, and the country will suffer a real disaster. From this, it can be inferred that Yu's thought is not only to advocate Kuomintang dictatorship, but also to advocate personal dictatorship, even monarchy. (5) Yu believes that ending tutelage and implementing constitutionalism is the proposition of the Communist Party and the Nationalist Party, and that it is supporting these two factions. In fact, the Communist Party does not care about tutelage or constitutionalism at all. Their means are straightforward. It is to revolutionize the Kuomintang. Although the Nationalist Party is more moderate, it is not very enthusiastic about this because they are also preparing revolutionary forces. Only teaching scholars like me who are unarmed and have a moderate attitude talk to the Kuomintang about tutelage and constitutionalism. (6) Yu opposes the democratic politics of the bourgeoisie. But what is the democratic politics of the bourgeoisie? What is non-bourgeois democratic politics? Yu did not explain it. But according to Yu's mind, we are afraid that we cannot even ask for the democratic politics of the bourgeoisie under the current tutelage of the Kuomintang. As for what Yu calls "revolutionary constitutionalism," it is simply deceiving the masses. (7) Yu bitterly destroys the Provisional Constitution of the Republic of China and Cao Kun's Constitution, but what about the National Covenant passed by the Kuomintang's national conference in 1931? Please review it, Mr. Yu. He scolds others as "warlords," as "bureaucrats," as "remnants of this era," and "dust of revolution." If Yu looks back at himself and at today's Kuomintang, what are they? Old bureaucratic politicians who rise up today to advocate constitutionalism, as Yu said, may not have the reason to seize power. But I dare not reject their resurrection. What I fear is that today's "warlords," "bureaucrats," "remnants of this era," and "dust of revolution" even want to seize power under the guise of tutelage and enter the grave. How sad! As for why I want to advocate ending tutelage and implementing constitutionalism, and my criticism of Sun Zhesheng's opinion, I will publish another article.

Free Talk

On the Free State of Ireland (Part 1) 206

— Kai Xu

There are many countries that occupy a small territory and enjoy equal international treatment. For example, the Free City of Danzig, which enjoys the dignity of independence with one city. Located among the powers, it can maintain its equilibrium. They guard their territory and do not invade each other. Another example is Monaco, whose capital is Monte Carlo, which is the gambling city. It maintains its independence by gambling. However, its territory is very small. If there is a riot in the country, no one can use artillery. Because the distance from one end to the other is very short. Every shot, if too large, is likely to fall into the territory of neighboring countries. Other examples include Bhutan and Nepal between China and India. Their area is only a few hundred square miles. As for the tragedy of being destroyed by huge countries, there were Poland in the past and India and Korea in recent times. Now Poland has been restored. Gandhi was born in India. Korea also has people like An Jung-geun. All of these are enough to represent the progressive spirit of their national restoration movement. The Irish Free State is adjacent to England. It is a small island. Shaped like a rabbit worshiping the moon. Among them, there are also great people. His name is Eamon de Valera. Abbreviated as de Valera. De Valera was born in the United States. His father was Spanish. His mother was Irish. Therefore, what he inherited from his parents was a strong and romantic personality. What he enjoyed in his early years was the free and equal air of the New World. Therefore, what he devoted his life to was Ireland's separation from the shackles of England. And the construction of an independent republic. He is not satisfied with the freedom within the cage. Now the freedom within the cage is still limited by the cage. It is not absolute freedom. The constitution of the Irish Free State. Article 17 clearly states that Irish officials should swear allegiance to the British Emperor. This is the cage of Irish freedom. De Valera has been immersed for ten years. Now he has become the head of the Free State. His first move is to cancel the oath of submission to the British Emperor. De Valera's proposal has passed the second reading in the Irish Parliament. The future success or failure is still unknown. War may break out between Britain and Ireland. However, the Irish people are strong. Not as weak as the Chinese. Their leaders are all unyielding men. Not like the rulers of our country who only know how to run after fame and fortune. Although Britain is determined not to give up its rights as a suzerain state. But Ireland is determined to fight to the end. Britain is exhausted. Unable to advance or retreat. How can it be like our government's declaration of long-term resistance today? Tomorrow, it will sign a humiliating agreement.

One Mistake, Then Another, Then Another 207

— Wang Haisusheng

The Xinhai Revolution. Invited the object of the revolution (Puyi, the deceased emperor of the Qing Dynasty) to step down. Replaced the signboard of the Great Qing Empire. Changed it to the Republic of China and treated the Qing imperial family favorably. Provided a pension. So that they could still live in the palace.

In the seventh year of the Republic of China. After Zhang Xun's attempt to restore Puyi with his pigtail failed. Puyi did not suffer any loss. He was treated favorably as before. In the thirteenth year, Feng Yuxiang returned to Beijing and only expelled this deposed emperor to Tianjin. Puyi, who lived in Tianjin, repeatedly wanted to travel abroad for further study. Our government did not pay attention to it. Did not raise funds for him to fulfill his long-cherished wish. Caused him to fall into the hands of the Japanese. Becoming a rare commodity.

After the September 18th Incident in the twentieth year of the Republic of China. The Japanese used the means of making use of waste. Kidnapped Puyi to the east. Our authorities knew about it beforehand. Did not prevent it. As a result, he was able to take charge of the new regime in Manchuria today.

Looking at the establishment of the puppet Republic of Manchuria in Changchun in March of this year, I felt touched. Looking back to check this old account. Speaking in terms of time. The period from the Xinhai Revolution to the seventh year of the Republic of China was one mistake. The period from the seventh year to the thirteenth year was another mistake. The period from the thirteenth year to the twentieth year was the third mistake. The period from the twentieth year to March of this year was the fourth mistake. With these four mistakes, a big mistake was made.

World Small Events Chronicle 208

— Haike

Hermit Using Coffin as Bed: In the forest near Bingham, Durham, England, there lives an old hermit named T. Thompson. He is seventy-five years old this year. Living his lonely life alone. He lives in a thatched cottage. There are only two chairs, a table, and a coffin in it. This coffin is his bed. He sleeps in it every night. Perhaps he knows that he will die soon. So he prepares for it in advance. If he dies suddenly at night. Then he is already sleeping in the coffin. There is no need for other procedures. According to him, he told a weekly reporter. He is indifferent to fame and fortune. He does not sink or swim with the world. He is only waiting for the arrival of death. Then everything can be ended. No matter what temptation there is in the world. He cannot be made to change his current life. In his youth, he participated in the Boer War. He received a pension. He can live on it. His companions are a cat. Several dogs. Several crows. And a few rabbits. Most of the food is hunted in the forest. He cooks and eats it himself. Such leisure and freedom are also enviable.

Thirteen Years of Submission 209

— Tao Zaidong

Free Talk is published at the end of the newspaper. Like the afterglow of a meeting. Like the end of a tune. Both solemn and humorous. Both elegant and popular. This is the work of the editor and the contributors. I have also been in the south for thirteen years. Graceful and charming. Like a young woman playing the zither. Such a long time has passed unknowingly. I have been contributing articles for the same number of years. Sparse and dense. Sentence by sentence. The so-called main theme is to advise the emperor. Those who speak are not guilty. Those who hear should be warned. Or it may be used to prove the present and cite the past. To follow what is right and correct what is wrong. As long as a word is beneficial to the people. Then the effort is not wasted. From now on. Eliminate national difficulties. Turn defeat into victory. The rise and fall of the country is the responsibility of everyone. Do not take the humble opinions of small newspapers lightly. Editors and contributors. Let's all work hard. Random words: Good to talk about the sky in Free Talk. Like singing a song and gathering immortals. Cherish every inch of time. How many thirteen years are there in life?

The Record of the Two Mansions in the Military Camp (50) 210

— Master of the Hall of Seeking Happiness

Chapter 6. Alas, pity for sharing a dream and being forced into a bed alliance. Still remembering first love, but breaking the promise at the window. At this point, An Yutian no longer had any resistance. Naturally, he agreed to everything and could not say half a no. Liang Xiaoyun was completely victorious and satisfied. She was so happy that her face was full of smiles. She immediately shrank back into the brocade quilt and also dragged An Yutian down. She gave him the sweetest and warmest kiss, saying, "Heaven has helped me. I have completely brought you into my arms. I hope you will trust me in everything from now on. I am definitely not boasting. I guarantee that our future is infinitely bright. I will help you become a great hero. We will always share the glory and wealth of this world. It is not in vain that I have put in so much effort today." There was nothing to say all night. The next day at noon, they got up together. She forced An Yutian to write the letter. In the letter, she openly explained Liang Xiaoyun's relationship and role. So that Li Wenxia knew that there was no way to recover. In addition, Liang Xiaoyun also signed a bank check. They were all sealed in the letter. An Yutian, against his will, sweating, did not say a word. He did everything. After lunch, Liang Xiaoyun dressed up slightly. She accompanied An Yutian to the apartment in a car, like escorting a prisoner. Supervising the relocation immediately. When entering the door, a porter greeted him and reported, "Mr. An, where did you go last night? That Miss Li came two or three times in the evening. She said that you had agreed to wait for her in the apartment. Why didn't you come back so late? She was very strange. Before leaving, she repeatedly told me. As soon as you come back, I will quickly call her. Who knew that you didn't come back all night. Her phone call came twice in the morning to ask. Do you want to call her first now?" An Yutian was just stunned. Liang Xiaoyun had already opened her mouth to the porter, "No need to call. Mr. An is busy moving. There is a letter left here for you. When Miss Li comes again, please give it to her personally." After giving the instructions, she opened her handbag. She handed over An Yutian's letter and took out a five-dollar bill to reward the porter. The porter was happily thanking her. Liang Xiaoyun was already urging An Yutian, "Hurry up and pack up. Don't let Li Wenxia catch you. It will be troublesome." An Yutian was flustered and also afraid of this. He was so anxious that he was at a loss. He grabbed around in the room. Liang Xiaoyun had to ask the porter to help. They hurriedly put the luggage and sundries in order. They didn't even have time to calculate the shop bill in detail. Liang Xiaoyun estimated and paid a few tens of dollars. He made it clear that whether there was a surplus or not, please send someone from the accounting office to Liang's house to settle the account later. They fled into the car with An Yutian and returned home. What happened next? I will write about it next time.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Wednesday, May 13, 21st Year of the Republic of China (No Additional Charge)

Discourse

Accumulate Small Amounts to Make a Lot 211

— Shi Ben

The Savior of the Unemployed... Giving Away Household Industries (Our company gives away household industries such as soap, dry batteries, cosmetics, and other crafts. We are responsible for success. Please attach postage stamps. We will send you the secret of the craft that will be tested, guaranteeing success and defeating deception.) Advertisements like these can be said to be in the advertising columns of various newspapers every day. Affected by the war, he is unemployed. He paces back and forth at home all day long, his brows furrowed, showing the pain of unemployment. Just when he has no way to go, he sees the advertisement above (The Savior of the Unemployed). After reading it, he feels that it does not cost a lot of money and the method is very simple. He is immediately overjoyed and hurriedly writes a very sincere letter, stating his willingness to learn crafts. He then buys the postage stamps and hurriedly seals them, goes to the postbox, and stuffs them inside. When he comes back from sending the letter, his face shows a joyful color, as if the happy god who saves the unemployed has descended on him. The previous frowning has become a thing of the past. Time passes so quickly. Since he sent this begging letter, half a month has passed. He looks forward to the arrival of this (Savior of the Unemployed) every day. He does not know that it is like a yellow crane, with no news at all. Although he has waited for half a month, the heat of hope has not diminished at all. He thinks that when people are unlucky, they must have encountered Hong Qiao. So he wrote a letter that was the same as before, bought the same postage stamps as before, and was afraid that sending it as a regular letter would cause it to be lost again. So he very cautiously went to the post office to add a registration, thinking that after this registered letter went, this (Savior of the Unemployed) would definitely be able to meet within a week. Who knew that he had waited for more than a month and still like a kite with a broken string, gone and never returned.

He was extremely angry. Calculating the losses, it also cost him some money. Thinking in his heart, how could he not receive it even after sending two letters? Moreover, the second letter was registered, so there was no way it could not be received. Then, why did he not receive a reply? Could it be that this advertisement (Savior of the Unemployed) was posted to deceive people out of money?! No, no, in order to deceive people out of these tiny postage stamps, he used a few dollars to post this advertisement, wouldn't that be killing the old cost? How could there be such a clumsy person in the world who does not know how to calculate? He thought about it again and again, but could not figure out a reason. He was suffocated, opened the newspaper of the day to read, ah...why is this advertisement still posted? Isn't it a long-term post? Alas, I understand, it must be using advertisements to cheat people out of money. As long as you think about it, there are many unemployed people in the society now. One person is deceived, it is limited, a thousand, ten thousand people are deceived, calculated, it is really not small. Alas, cheating the unemployed out of money is truly killing people without regard for the bloody smell.

Science

Colorless Ink 214

— Jian

Ordinary ink is written on paper, and the handwriting can be recognized immediately, which is too public. There are also various colorless inks, which leave no traces on the paper. Further procedures are required for the handwriting to appear. This is often used for communication in situations where it cannot be made public.

(1) Blue: Use cobalt dichloride (CoCl2), one part dissolved in eighteen parts of water. Write on paper with this solution. After drying, heat it slightly by the fire, and the blue handwriting will appear. Cool it down again, and it will disappear and cannot be recognized.

(2) Brown: Dissolve two parts of yellow blood salt in water. Write on paper. After drying, use a brush dipped in copper sulfate to paint it, and the handwriting will become brown.

(3) Yellow: Write on paper with copper dichloride solution. The yellow handwriting will appear after heating. Cool it down, and it will disappear. Also, dissolve four parts of potassium chloride and four parts of copper sulfate in thirty parts of water. Write on paper, dry it, and heat it, and the yellow handwriting will also appear.

(4) Gold: Write on paper with sodium gold chloride solution (but it should not be too light). After drying, use a brush dipped in 10% oxalic acid solution to paint it again and again. After drying, press it flat with a press, and beautiful gold characters will appear.

(5) Green: Dissolve two parts of cobalt dichloride and one part of nickel dichloride in fifty parts of water. Write on paper, dry it, and heat it, and the green handwriting will appear. Or use potassium chlorate solution to write, and after drying, paint it with copper sulfate solution, and the green handwriting will also appear, but it will never disappear.

(6) Red: Write with sodium gold chloride solution on paper. After drying, use a pen dipped in tin salt to paint it, (tin salt SnCl2 should not be too concentrated), and red handwriting can be obtained.

(7) Black: Use a brush dipped in concentrated lead acetate solution to write on paper. After drying, fumigate it with hydrogen sulfide, and black handwriting will appear. Also, use a brush to mix the white juice that flows out of the onion when cutting an onion and write it on paper. Heat it after drying and black characters will also appear.

Questions of Sexuality

Eating Tofu 215

— Wu Hezhou

Two college-student-like young men were talking: (How's life been lately?) (Still just messing around in school, wandering around outside school. Do you come here often?) (Yes, I come often.) (Probably here to "eat tofu," huh!)

Their conversation was taking place in a corner of ×× Park. At the time, I was also idly relaxing, so I heard them very clearly. However, I didn't quite understand the noun "eat tofu," and I didn't know what the "object of the action" referred to. I figured it was probably some kind of slang. I just heard them continue to say: (Your methods are clever, I imagine you must have a good harvest.) (Not very smooth, really the Misses are too cunning.) (But you get teased by them, right?) (That's right, last night I even got a curse from a CirlStudent saying "old three"!) (Haha...you were always a famous "hungry ghost"!) (We're comrades, no need to say more.)

Hearing this, I understood a lot in my heart. Looking at their well-dressed figures, I felt a wave of emotion, so I left them. According to the results of asking around, I learned that "eating tofu" is a synonym for "pursuing women."

I occasionally think of Yuan Shikai's downfall due to the signing of the Twenty-One Demands, and I can't help but break out in a cold sweat for the government authorities who signed the humiliating agreement!

A Corner of Society

At the Deyilou Restaurant 217

— Yiping

▲ One of the City God Temple Image Records

One day, I fulfilled an appointment with someone to go to the Deyilou Restaurant in the City God Temple. I searched all over the second and third floors but couldn't find my friend's shadow. Because we had agreed that whoever arrived first would wait, I ordered a pot of tea and sat quietly. I sat there idly for two hours. (My friend failed to show up) confirmed for me the saying "(Chinese people are good at consuming time)," which was one of the weaknesses of Chinese people mentioned by a certain foreigner at a news media banquet.

They all had their left legs crossed over their right, swaying triumphantly, holding newspapers in their hands, scrutinizing them as carefully as if they were looking up words in a dictionary, or lighting cigarettes, tilting their heads back, and reclining in rattan chairs, staring blankly at the white smoke they exhaled, like Newton studying why apples fall from trees without wind. Most strangely, there were a few dazed tea drinkers, half-asleep, as if perchance some unusual sound were to occur, such as a woman's shout, they would open their eyes and look around. I later mentioned this to a friend, who said it was much cheaper than renting a room!

If four or five people came together, they could, of course, chat tirelessly for hours. In my two hours of imprisonment, based on my subjective observation, I couldn't find a single tea drinker who had truly come for the (tea). It was like the clock shop on Fourth Road having clocks, but actually, a crowd was gathered to listen to the radio broadcast.

Reason

A Nosy Foreign Lady 218

— Bai Tao

The day before yesterday afternoon, a foreign lady and I boarded the same tram. This foreign lady was old and stooped, her hair snow-white. She took a seat in the seam of people across from me. At that time, I was very tired from walking, so I picked an empty seat and sat down. After one stop, a pot-bellied businessman and a woman boarded. The pot-bellied businessman was sharp-eyed and quick-footed. With three steps and two strides, he sat down next to me, crossed his legs, and turned to look out the window at the excitement. This woman who failed to get a seat had no choice but to stand there, waiting for a vacancy. The foreign lady across from me looked displeased, sniffed, and muttered something. I had already guessed her intention. Sure enough, she raised the cane in her hand and waved it at the businessman, signaling him to sit properly and make room for the woman. But he ignored her, put his foot down, and continued to look out the window. The foreign lady got angry, muttering incessantly, but I couldn't hear what she was saying. A compatriot with a mustache sneered behind her back, saying: (What a nosy old woman!)

Not long after, (wow) a sound suddenly came from next to the foreign lady. I hurriedly looked over to see what had happened. One of the Chinese women next to her spat a mouthful of phlegm, and (cough...) continued to spray it in her face. The foreign lady was furious, wrinkled her nose, and muttered loudly. She was warning her not to spit anywhere, and if she had to spit, she could spit out the window. Unexpectedly, this muttering caused the Chinese woman to (giggle) laugh non-stop, and the compatriots around her also laughed uproariously. The foreign lady was so angry that she stretched her neck and kept swallowing saliva. I silently looked at the crowd. I wanted to laugh, but I couldn't bring myself to laugh.

Yes! What a nosy foreign old woman! We Chinese people mind our own business and never bother with such matters!

Post-War Foundations 220

— Wu

Not long ago, this place was still filled with the earth-shattering sounds of cannons, but now it is the un-rhythmic sound of breaking stones that continues. The sun shines on every crack in this tile kiln, and a strong, fermented, musty smell rises straight up. The women who are breaking stones breathe in this debilitating air, using every last bit of their strength.

They are constantly hammering large stones into countless small pieces, each with a pile of this size in front of them. Hammer, hammer, hammer! Using all their consciousness and strength, hammer, hammer, hammer, hammering until sparks fly. The hard iron hammer strikes the hard stones, producing a crisp sound like the clashing of skeletons.

An engineer, unfolding his drawings, walks in from outside, followed by a large belly, walking unevenly as if lame, with a fine cigar in his mouth. The engineer points to the map, explaining his architectural plans. The large belly only makes buzzing sounds!

But this place is, after all, too noisy. Besides the sound of the iron hammer hitting the stones, there is the "heave-ho" of the workers driving piles in front, the roar of trucks transporting steel beams in the back, and a child in the corner tugging at the skirt of the stone-breaking woman's mother and crying. So the large belly couldn't help but run over and point at the stone-breaking woman's mother, shouting, (You old woman, you come to work, why do you bring a child here to cry? It's disturbing everyone!) (Sir, because he's hungry... I'm really sorry,) The old woman slapped the child's face and pleaded as if crying. Fortunately, the engineer came to invite him to another construction site, otherwise, the old woman would definitely have been kicked out. But the child cried even harder, and tears involuntarily streamed down the mother's face.

The sun continued to shine madly, and the sound of hammering continued. What has the post-war peace given them? Just this and nothing more.

Lack of Public Spirit 221

— Yun Zong

On the wall is written (No Urinating Here), but a shop assistant is letting his "tap water" flow freely at the base of the wall. Although there is a sign in the public bus that says (No Smoking), it is common to encounter a gentleman reading a newspaper while puffing away on a cigarette.

A group of college students in a movie theater, seeing the wonderful expressions on the screen, cannot help but applaud like thunder, their cheers shaking the roof, forgetting completely the two sentences written on both sides of the stage, (Please Do Not Applaud) (Please Do Not Make Noise).

The appellant's claim in the aforementioned portion is rejected. The litigation costs for the first and second instances shall be borne by the appellee.

▲ Wufu Company Rice Shop vs. Wang Hong, Meal Shop, Debt Case (Main Text): The defendant should pay the plaintiff 136.10 yuan. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲ Tongtaisheng Hao, Zhang Jingfu vs. Shi Changtai Zhuang, Bao Yong, Debt Case (Main Text): The defendant should repay the plaintiff 288 taels, 7 mace, and 5 candareens, plus interest at an annual rate of 0.5% from September 17th of the 20th year of the Republic of China until the day of execution. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲ Kaiyi Company vs. Ai A'na'er, Rent Arrears and Eviction Case (Main Text): The defendant should repay the plaintiff's rent of 283 taels and 6 fen, and vacate the house. The plaintiff's remaining claims are rejected. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant for six-sevenths and the plaintiff for one-seventh. This case should be subject to provisional execution regarding the eviction portion.

▲ Lan Tang vs. Zhu A'san, Goods Payment Case (Main Text): The defendant should repay the plaintiff's goods payment of 60 taels and 7 mace, 5 candareens, plus interest calculated at an annual rate of 0.5% from April 16th of the Republic of China until the day of repayment. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲ Wang Yuhe Wine Shop, Zhong Peiquan vs. Sheng Shun Laundry Shop Owner, Chen Zuocai, Rent Arrears and Eviction Case (Main Text): The defendant should repay the plaintiff's rent of 456 taels and 2 mace and vacate the house. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant. Provisional execution is not permitted in this case.

▲ Bai Shengersheng vs. Hu Caixing, Loan Case (Main Text): The defendant Hu Caixing should repay the plaintiff 60 yuan. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲ Wang Changgeng vs. Gu Xiangsheng, Loan Case (Main Text): The defendant Gu Xiangsheng should repay the plaintiff 300 yuan, plus interest at a monthly rate of 1.5% from June 17th of the 19th year of the Republic of China until the day of repayment. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲ Ha Li Lang vs. Wu Yisheng, Loan Case (Main Text): The defendant Wu Yisheng should repay the plaintiff 50 yuan. If he fails to fulfill the obligation, the defendant Wang Shaoshan is responsible for compensating on his behalf. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant Wu Yisheng.

▲ A'mu Sheng vs. Hu Zhensheng et al., Debt Case (Main Text): The defendant Wu Dajun should repay the plaintiff 200 yuan. If he cannot repay, the defendants Hu Zhensheng and Wang Zhaofeng are jointly responsible for compensating. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant Wu Dajun.

▲ Zhaochang Money Shop vs. Chen Caixing, Debt Case (Main Text): The defendant should repay the Zhaochang Money Shop managed by the plaintiff 298 yuan, 1 jiao, 9 fen, and 7 li, plus interest at an annual rate of 0.5% from January 30th of the 19th year of the Republic of China until the day of execution. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲ Ma Ke vs. Zeng Guangxu, Debt Case (Main Text): The defendant should repay the plaintiff 681 taels of silver, of which 300 taels from May 16th of the 20th year of the Republic of China, another 300 taels from June 16th of the same year, and 81 taels from July 16th of the same year, all calculated with interest at an annual rate of 0.5% until the day of repayment. The plaintiff's remaining claims are rejected. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲ Shao Maike vs. Ekensitan, Compensation Case (Main Text): The defendant should compensate the plaintiff 1,463 taels and 5 mace of silver, plus interest at an annual rate of 0.5% from July 21st of the 20th year of the Republic of China until the day of execution. The tea trading contract stipulated by both parties is permitted to be terminated. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲ Shunhe Firm vs. Song Youjun, Debt Case (Main Text): The defendant should repay the plaintiff 38 yuan, 7 jiao, and 7 fen. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant. This case should be subject to provisional execution.

▲ Xie Lai Sheng vs. Zong Linsheng et al., Loan Case (Main Text): The defendant Zong Linsheng should repay the plaintiff 290 yuan. If he fails to fulfill the obligation, the defendant Yang Miaogen is responsible for compensating on his behalf. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant Zong Linsheng.

▲ Bai Te Baixin vs. Zhang Linji et al., Loan Case (Main Text): The defendant Zhang Linji should repay the plaintiff 200 yuan. If he fails to fulfill the obligation, the defendant Wang Sanhe is responsible for compensating on his behalf. Also, the defendant Zhang Linji should repay the plaintiff 400 yuan. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant Zhang Linji.

▲ Yaqin Sheng vs. Sun Naizao et al., Loan Case (Main Text): The defendant Sun Naizao should repay the plaintiff 180 yuan. If he fails to fulfill the obligation, the defendant Cao Yongsheng is responsible for compensating on his behalf. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant Sun Naizao.

▲ Criminal Second Instance Judgments

Lha Youzhang vs. Lu Jiefu, Appeal Against Fraud Decision (Main Text): The appeal is rejected.

▲ Xia Keliang vs. Wang Xufang et al., Appeal Against Fraud Decision (Main Text): The appeal is rejected.

▲ Chao Ziyang et al., Appeal Against Larceny Decision (Main Text): The original judgment is revoked. This court will conduct the first instance trial. Chao Ziyang is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for embezzlement of items held in the course of business. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be counted as two days equivalent to one day of imprisonment. Chen Zhangshi is sentenced to a fine of fifty yuan for joint embezzlement. If the fine is not paid through compulsory execution, two yuan is equivalent to one day of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day equivalent to two yuan of the fine.

▲ Xu Jichang vs. Huang Runzhi, Appeal Against Fraud and False Accusation Decision (Main Text): The original judgment is revoked regarding the sentence of Ji Xuchang. Xu Jichang is found not guilty. The remaining appeals are rejected.

Notice for Second Reduced Price Auction: It has been found that this court is executing the case of Xu Pying endangering the Republic of China. The movable property owned by Xu Pying has been seized, appraised, and auctioned. As no one bid by the deadline, the minimum price is now reduced by 10% of the original price. The auction date is set for May 21st. The court will dispatch a clerk along with police officers to the location of the movable property to conduct the auction. All residents who wish to purchase this movable property should come to the Clerk's Office of this court for instructions in order to be led to the location to inspect the property before participating in the auction on the scheduled date. If there are two or more bidders, the person with the highest bid will be the purchaser. The full price should be paid on the spot, and the auctioned property will be given to the purchaser for receipt. All residents are hereby notified. Special notice is hereby given. (Details are as follows) (1) Auction Subject: Movable Property (2) Location of the Property: This Court (3) Minimum Price: 18 yuan, 7 jiao, 5 fen, 1 li, and 5 hao (4) Location for Reviewing Records: Clerk's Office of this Court (5) Execution Clerk: Zhu Guangzhao

Shanghai Second Special District Local Court 225

▲Criminal Judgment: Police Department vs. Liu Haiqing et al. for Theft (Main Text) Liu Haiqing and Wang Mingde are each sentenced to one year of imprisonment for the three crimes of destroying a wall, trespassing into a residence at night, and theft, with a total of one year and two months of imprisonment. Chen Fubao and Lu Er'e are each sentenced to six months of imprisonment for knowingly buying stolen goods. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be counted at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. ▲Police Department vs. Mao Afu et al. for Theft and Stolen Goods (Main Text) Mao Afu is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for theft. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be counted at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Du Shiwen is fined 30 yuan for knowingly buying stolen goods. If he is unable to pay the fine, he will be detained for one day for every two yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be counted at a rate of one day for every two yuan of the fine. ▲Police Department vs. Ye Zhangshi et al. for Assault and Damage (Main Text) Ye Zhangshi is sentenced to one year and one month of imprisonment for the crime of injuring the body of a collateral senior relative, and two months of imprisonment for the crime of damage, with a total of one year and two months of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be counted at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. The incidental civil litigation part is transferred to the civil court of this court for trial. ▲Police Department vs. Wang Xuegui for Theft (Main Text) Wang Xuegui is sentenced to 30 days of detention for theft. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be counted at a rate of two days for one day of detention. ▲Police Department vs. Ding Shaoshan for Opium Case (Main Text) Ding Shaoshan is fined 60 yuan for possessing opium paraphernalia. If he is unable to pay the fine, he will be detained for one day for every two yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be counted at a rate of one day for every two yuan of the fine. The opium pipe, opium lamp, opium needle, opium tray, etc., are all confiscated and burned. ▲Police Department vs. Rong Baoqin for Opium Case (Main Text) Rong Baole is fined 100 yuan for possessing opium paraphernalia. This public notice is hereby issued to the defendants Tang Mouwu and Zhang Haiqing. ▲Public Notice: Yuansheng Money Shop Chen Hongqing Pawn Case. This court has scheduled a public hearing for 9:00 AM on June 3rd. In addition to appointing lawyer Chen Honglai as the special agent for the defendant Chen Hongqing, the defendant is ordered to appear in court on schedule to argue the case without delay. This public notice is hereby issued to the defendant Chen Hongqing. ▲Judgment: Bai Jinsheng vs. Chen Wantao for Loan Case (Main Text) The defendant should repay the plaintiff's loan of 200 yuan. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant. The defendant Chen Wantao is hereby notified. ▲Criminal Judgment: Pan Caisheng for Theft Case (Main Text) Pan Caisheng is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for committing theft during a disaster. The number of days of detention will be counted at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. ▲Xie Agen for Theft Case (Main Text) Xie Agen is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for trespassing into a residence at night and committing theft. The number of days of detention will be counted at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. ▲Zhao Nanjing for Robbery Case (Main Text) Zhao Nanjing is sentenced to three months of imprisonment for robbing property belonging to others. The number of days of detention will be counted at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. ▲Ren Zhennan for Fraud Appeal Case (Main Text) The original judgment on Ren Zhennan's sentencing is revoked. Ren Zhennan is sentenced to eight months of imprisonment for obtaining property from others by fraudulent means with the intention of unlawful possession for himself. The number of days of detention will be counted at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. The incidental civil lawsuit appeal is rejected. ▲Criminal Judgment: Sun Weizhan et al. for Robbery Case (Main Text) Sun Weishang and Wu Baosheng are each sentenced to three months of imprisonment for jointly robbing property belonging to others. The number of days of detention will be counted at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Qiao Wanjin is found not guilty. ▲Ma Zhenshan for Opium Case (Main Text) Ma Zhenshan is sentenced to six months of imprisonment and a fine of 60 yuan for possessing opium substitutes with the intention of selling them. If the fine is not paid after compulsory execution, it will be converted to detention at a rate of one yuan per day. The number of days of detention will be counted at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Ninety-eight boxes of red pills are confiscated and burned.
